        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980378119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14417069706129597279">The Lost World takes place six years after the Jurassic Park incident, and just like in the movie version, Dr. Alan Grant and Dr. Sattler did not return but Dr. Ian Malcolm does return for his role. The Lost World was an entertaining read, although I'll say not as good as Jurassic Park, for a number of reasons, but I won't go into all of them. I found myself skipping through some of the unnecessary parts that weren't really important to the story but when I came to some of the important parts I </span>
  <span id="freeText14417069706129597279" style="display:none">The Lost World takes place six years after the Jurassic Park incident, and just like in the movie version, Dr. Alan Grant and Dr. Sattler did not return but Dr. Ian Malcolm does return for his role. The Lost World was an entertaining read, although I'll say not as good as Jurassic Park, for a number of reasons, but I won't go into all of them. I found myself skipping through some of the unnecessary parts that weren't really important to the story but when I came to some of the important parts I was hooked. <br /><br />A lot of new dinosaurs are introduced to us in this book that were not in Jurassic Park, a lot of them I'd never even heard of, some of them I even needed to Google them to see if they were even real since this book was fiction, and they were real. The book was very different from the movie, and to me there didn't really seem to be any similarities accept the character of Sarah Harding who was played by Julianne Moore (Who I've always had a big crush on, HAHA) in the movie.<br /><br />Some parts of the story seemed to drag but it also did have some really nail-biting parts and many twists and turns throughout. Like I said, it's not up there with Jurassic Park but still worth reading.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14417069706129597279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1915103286?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51309506-a-s?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1915103286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer521482457000294724"><p>
  <a href='https://thebandarblog.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <br/>
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469289873i/19802032.png' alt='the bandar blog' width='390' height='90' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</p>In case you missed it, not too long ago <a href='https://thebandarblog.com/2017/01/27/jurassic-park-review/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>I was raving about <em>Jurassic Park</em>.</a> I hadn't read the book before and was instantly obsessed. Needless to say, I was quick to pick up <em>The Lost World</em>, because sequels = more dinosaurs. While I didn't end up obsessing over <em>The Lost World</em> quite as much as JP, the 12-year-old boy in me was still satisfied by T-Rex scares, human-eating dinosaurs, and terrifying AF raptors.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/> 
  <strong>What I didn't like <em>quite</em> as much:</strong>
 <br/> <br/> 	 It seemed just a <strong>tad-bit more sc</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText521482457000294724" style="display:none"><p>
  <a href="https://thebandarblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <br>
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469289873i/19802032.png" alt="the bandar blog" width="390" height="90" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p>In case you missed it, not too long ago <a href="https://thebandarblog.com/2017/01/27/jurassic-park-review/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">I was raving about <em>Jurassic Park</em>.</a> I hadn't read the book before and was instantly obsessed. Needless to say, I was quick to pick up <em>The Lost World</em>, because sequels = more dinosaurs. While I didn't end up obsessing over <em>The Lost World</em> quite as much as JP, the 12-year-old boy in me was still satisfied by T-Rex scares, human-eating dinosaurs, and terrifying AF raptors.<br><br><br><br><br> 
  <strong>What I didn't like <em>quite</em> as much:</strong>
 <br> <br> 	 It seemed just a <strong>tad-bit more science-y</strong>. Lots and lots of talk about things I personally didn't care as much about. <em>Um, excuse me, but when is the T-Rex gonna show up?</em> <br> 	 <strong>The plot just wasn't <em>as</em> fun for me </strong>(it's still good, though!). JP is all about this cool new place- everything is optimistic and exciting. <em>Then</em> it all spirals out of control and gets crappy. This book is about perhaps finding the remnants of Jurassic Park, so as a reader I knew everything wasn't going to be all hunky-dory this time. I <em>knew</em> it was going to be bad. I <strong>missed that false sense of security</strong> that JP had -- it made things slightly more fun for me. <br> <br> 
  <strong>What was freaking awesome:</strong>
 <br> <br> 	 <strong>THE T-REX(s, YES PLURAL)</strong><strong>.</strong> I'm seriously obsessed. Every time I would be listening to this audiobook and it'd start describing loud crashing sounds or big steps that caused the ground to vibrate I'd get so freaking giddy. <br> 	 There's all sorts of <strong>fun people-running-away-from-dinosaurs bits</strong> in this. It's exciting and scary and perfect! <br> 	 The <strong>enemies get what they deserve</strong> (and it's usually in the form of munching dinosaur teeth). <br> <br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474030346i/20545245.png" alt="" width="291" height="51" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474030346i/20545246.png" alt="" width="34" height="35" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474030346i/20545246.png" alt="" width="34" height="35" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474030346i/20545246.png" alt="" width="34" height="35" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474030346i/20545246.png" alt="" width="34" height="35" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <strong><br>The bottom line? READ THESE BOOKS. They're too much fun to pass up.</strong>
  <br>
  <br>
</p> 
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490270629i/22296852._SY540_.jpg" alt="the lost world michael crichton" width="437" height="495" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <br> 
  <strong>
    <a href="https://thebandarblog.com/2017/01/27/jurassic-park-review/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">See my rave review of <em>Jurassic Park</em> here!</a>
  </strong>
 <br> 
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474030346i/20545248.png" alt="" width="221" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <strong>Have you read this one? How did you feel it compared to <em>Jurassic Park</em>? How is the movie? I haven't seen it yet but will probably watch it, because dinosaurs.</strong>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679419464" href="/book/show/672988.The_Lost_World">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47010576-samantha-w?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47010576-samantha-w?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47010576-samantha-w?shelf=150books2020">150books2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47010576-samantha-w?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47010576-samantha-w?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3360732396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8001900724715467293">Honestly, who doesn't enjoy a good book about dinosaurs? <br/><br/>I enjoyed this book just as much as the first one. The science was interesting, and based on the first book feels believable. (Bc corporations are greedy and will do sneaky shit to make money....) <br/><br/>I liked the characters just as much this time around, and glad that Dodgson got what he deserved. If you like the Jurassic Park movies, you will probably also enjoy these books.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_32334792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32334792" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1502792-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344876203p2/1502792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32334792?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/1502792-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32334792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12526563674296983545">Jurassic Park was pretty good, but this book was rather poor. It reads like a bad movie. The author is so intent upon pushing Chaos Theory upon the reader that he often forces the characters to behave way, way, WAY out of their habits in order to force things to go wrong.<br/><br/>People suddenly do really stupid things. People forget that they have weapons. All attempts to prepare for a situation automatically fail, because it's completely impossible (not just improbable) for a prepared individual to act</span>
  <span id="freeText12526563674296983545" style="display:none">Jurassic Park was pretty good, but this book was rather poor. It reads like a bad movie. The author is so intent upon pushing Chaos Theory upon the reader that he often forces the characters to behave way, way, WAY out of their habits in order to force things to go wrong.<br /><br />People suddenly do really stupid things. People forget that they have weapons. All attempts to prepare for a situation automatically fail, because it's completely impossible (not just improbable) for a prepared individual to actually be ready to face the situation he was preparing for.<br /><br />Even the identities of the characters were engineerd to be movie-friendly. As he wrote this book, the author knew that he would have a film deal upon completion. He constructed the story so that Hollywood wouldn't have to work too hard to dumb it down.<br /><br />I won't spoil the ending, but you should know that it was stupid. It involved the best animal scientists in the world making a mistake that would have been caught by the folks at your local zoo.<br /><br />It was kind of like watching people play craps in an alley with a math professor. Each time the dice are thrown, the guy runs forward, picks them up and carefully sets them down with a less favorable result, all the while ranting about how random everything is.<br /><br />In a situation like that, the other guys in the alley would have just beaten the tar out of him. That's what I wanted to do when I read this.<br /><br />It's a dumb book which hides behind a bunch of big, smart words. Don't bother with it. If you watch the movie you'll at least get to see the dinosaurs running around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12526563674296983545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DiJcc3GBB+DcAQhThcbQeGQbJiBhVGj08bc624L7mAc0BDWhyt/OiHsqvDJyM9qnskTB6K/Z5pOqyXxqT7hqnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hn6EnXBsn4L9eUlxC/vvyS7nYrC39H0eSfoIFvAzYJm8WO1PyzJW6lpS/RD8DuUW+LiFeHl583kShE6nPXCSAw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Max Brooks, driven by the urgency of preserving the acid-etched first-hand experiences of the survivors from those apocalyptic years, traveled across the United States of America and throughout the world, from decimated cities that once teemed with upwards of thirty million souls to the most remote and inhospitable areas of the planet. He recorded the testimony of men, women, and sometimes children who came face-to-face with the living, or at least the undead, hell of that dreadful time. World War Z is the result. Never before have we had access to a document that so powerfully conveys the depth of fear and horror, and also the ineradicable spirit of resistance, that gripped human society through the plague years.\n\nRanging from the now infamous village of New Dachang in the United Federation of China, where the epidemiological trail began with the twelve-year-old Patient Zero, to the unnamed northern forests where untold numbers sought a terrible and temporary refuge in the cold, to the United States of Southern Africa, where the Redeker Plan provided hope for humanity at an unspeakable price, to the west-of-the-Rockies redoubt where the North American tide finally started to turn, this invaluable chronicle reflects the full scope and duration of the Zombie War.\n\nMost of all, the book captures with haunting immediacy the human dimension of this epochal event. Facing the often raw and vivid nature of these personal accounts requires a degree of courage on the part of the reader, but the effort is invaluable because, as Mr. Brooks says in his introduction, &quot;By excluding the human factor, aren\'t we risking the kind of personal detachment from history that may, heaven forbid, lead us one day to repeat it?       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">About Michael Crichton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1359042651p3/5194.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
13,859
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16257525420738133957">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On' title='Odds On' rel='nofollow noopener'>Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange' title='John Lange' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas' title='Michael Douglas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael Doug</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16257525420738133957" style="display:none">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On" title="Odds On" rel="nofollow noopener">Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange" title="John Lange" rel="nofollow noopener">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Douglas</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/607284.Jeffery_Hudson" title="Jeffery Hudson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeffery Hudson</a>. His novel <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7663.A_Case_of_Need" title="A Case of Need" rel="nofollow noopener">A Case of Need</a>
</i> won the Edgar Award in 1969. Popular throughout the world, he has sold more than 200 million books. His novels have been translated into thirty-eight languages, and thirteen have been made into films.<br /><br />Michael Crichton passed away from lymphoma in 2008. He was 66 years old.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16257525420738133957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1212784-the-lost-world">Quotes from The Lost World</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;What makes you think human beings are sentient and aware? There's no evidence for it. Human beings never think for themselves, they find it too uncomfortable. For the most part, members of our species simply repeat what they are told-and become upset if they are exposed to any different view. The characteristic human trait is not awareness but conformity, and the characteristic result is religious warfare. Other animals fight for territory or food; but, uniquely in the animal kingdom, human beings fight for their 'beliefs.' The reason is that beliefs guide behavior which has evolutionary importance among human beings. But at a time when our behavior may well lead us to extinction, I see no reason to assume we have any awareness at all. We are stubborn, self-destructive conformists. Any other view of our species is just a self-congratulatory delusion. Next question.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/52994-what-makes-you-think-human-beings-are-sentient-and-aware">402 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;All your life people will tell you things. And most of the time, probably ninety-five percent of the time, what they'll tell you will be wrong.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/154085-all-your-life-people-will-tell-you-things-and-most">198 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/1212784-the-lost-world">More quotes&hellip;</a>
